  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3037d942-061a-4799-b626-521c8dfb2c61'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer16174923416418285221"><br/>For the five teens who modeled as Disney Hologram Imaging hosts, life is beginning to settle down when an intriguing video arrives to Philby's computer at school. It's a call for action: the Overtakers, a group of Disney villains, seem to be plotting to attempt a rescue of two of their leaders, both of whom the Disney Imagineers have hidden away somewhere following a viole</span>
  <span id="freeText16174923416418285221" style="display:none"><br />For the five teens who modeled as Disney Hologram Imaging hosts, life is beginning to settle down when an intriguing video arrives to Philby's computer at school. It's a call for action: the Overtakers, a group of Disney villains, seem to be plotting to attempt a rescue of two of their leaders, both of whom the Disney Imagineers have hidden away somewhere following a violent encounter in Epcot. A staged attack by new Overtakers at Downtown Disney, startles the group.<br /><br />One of their own, Charlene, is acting strange of late. Has she tired of her role as a Kingdom Keeper or is there something more sinister at play? When caught sneaking into Epcot as her DHI, acting strictly against the group's rules, Finn and Philby take action.<br /><br />Has the "impossible" occurred? Have the Overtakers created their own holograms? Have they found a way to "jump" from the Virtual Maintenance Network onto the Internet, and if so, what does that mean for the safety of the parks, and the spread and reach of the Overtakers? Are they recruiting an army from <i>outside</i> the parks?<br /><br />A dark cloud in the Kingdom Keeper era is unfolding, and with dissention in their own ranks, it's unclear if there's any chance of escape.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11669055439854150528">Review originally published on <a href='http://mybookshelfisready.tumblr.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Bookshelf is Ready</a>.<br/><br/>3.25 Stars<br/><br/>This is the fourth book in Ridley Pearson's Kingdom Keepers series, and like the previous 3 it starts out strong, has a really boring middle, and an interesting finish. The first hundred or so pages are fast and exciting, and I usually read those in one sitting. There's just always a huge lull in the middle. Granted, it's an action-packed lull, but it's also an info dump at the same time. For the last three books, I've seriously cont</span>
  <span id="freeText11669055439854150528" style="display:none">Review originally published on <a href="http://mybookshelfisready.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Bookshelf is Ready</a>.<br /><br />3.25 Stars<br /><br />This is the fourth book in Ridley Pearson's Kingdom Keepers series, and like the previous 3 it starts out strong, has a really boring middle, and an interesting finish. The first hundred or so pages are fast and exciting, and I usually read those in one sitting. There's just always a huge lull in the middle. Granted, it's an action-packed lull, but it's also an info dump at the same time. For the last three books, I've seriously contemplated giving up right in the middle because it just seems like so much filler. But when I see them through to the end, it <i>almost</i> seems worth it.</span>

<div id="review_168456740" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168456740" />
    <a title="Dreamhopelove888" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5444947-dreamhopelove888"><img alt="Dreamhopelove888" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305646865p2/5444947.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168456740?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dreamhopelove888" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dreamhopelove888" href="/user/show/5444947-dreamhopelove888">Dreamhopelove888</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168456740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2789106874092278417"> This series has always been one of my favorites. I might be bias because I LOVE Disney World but i think the writing is quite magical also. In this book, Power Play, Pearson, in my opinion, makes the characters more demensional and real. I feel like I know them personally now that i have just finished this book. THere is so much to say about this book so i will just get on with it!!<br/> Because these books are centered around Disney, they are very differnt then other books. The settings are through</span>
  <span id="freeText2789106874092278417" style="display:none"> This series has always been one of my favorites. I might be bias because I LOVE Disney World but i think the writing is quite magical also. In this book, Power Play, Pearson, in my opinion, makes the characters more demensional and real. I feel like I know them personally now that i have just finished this book. THere is so much to say about this book so i will just get on with it!!<br /> Because these books are centered around Disney, they are very differnt then other books. The settings are throughout the wonderful, magical parks! I feel in this book, Pearson really incorparated a deeper look into the parks and how they function. This really kept my interest because as I said, I Love Disney. He also brought in more of the Disney characters we all love... and hate for that matter. It was a nice suprise to put Ariel in the story. I was literally beaming when she saved Willa from the lake in Hollywood Studios! Pearson did a great job to portray the Disney characters as they act in their movies but in more modern ways. <br /> The action in this book was spectacular. It was really intense specially towards the last half of the book. I was not expecting kids to be brought in by the OT's and on top of that they all had menacing green eyes?!?! The kingdom Keepers really had it tough throughout the book! The thing that was most suspenseful for me was the jailbreak scene with Finn and Wayne! <br /> Speaking of Wayne, it was nice to see him person in this book. It was a nice refresher because when we do hear from him, it is by video or special messages.<br /> On "bump in the road" for the fourth kingdom keepers book was the technological talk by Phibly. At times, the book was a little hard to follow because of the depth of the technology knowledge that we needed to follow. I found that I just had to keep reading and try to understand what was going on as the action played out. That is my only complaint about the book and it is so minor that it does not affect my rating of the book.<br /> Can't wait for the next book. On a Cruise ship?!?! I'm pumped!! Way to go Pearson and thanks for signing my book!! All the more special!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2789106874092278417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167763794" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167763794" />
    <a title="Drew Graham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3346313-drew-graham"><img alt="Drew Graham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280704207p2/3346313.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167763794?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew Graham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew Graham" href="/user/show/3346313-drew-graham">Drew Graham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3346313-drew-graham?shelf=me">me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167763794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5311082893361010060">*sigh*<br/><br/>Where do I begin now that I've finished?<br/><br/>The toil over, at least for now (perhaps forever?... The fifth book is supposed to be released next year). I think this book was better than the last two, for two reasons: 1) It was more than a hundred pages shorter, and 2) There were finally more Disney characters, good and bad. The idea that there might actually be good guys in this world is finally explored, but sadly still mishandled. Some of them are described so laughably different that there's</span>
  <span id="freeText5311082893361010060" style="display:none">*sigh*<br /><br />Where do I begin now that I've finished?<br /><br />The toil over, at least for now (perhaps forever?... The fifth book is supposed to be released next year). I think this book was better than the last two, for two reasons: 1) It was more than a hundred pages shorter, and 2) There were finally more Disney characters, good and bad. The idea that there might actually be good guys in this world is finally explored, but sadly still mishandled. Some of them are described so laughably different that there's no way in the world the kids in the book would recognize them as their movie or ride counterparts, let alone the kids reading. For all the in-depth and backstage research the author was apparently allowed, he still manages to get in a whole lot of inaccuracies about the parks and characters (Big Ben in Epcot's UK? And since when is Pluto a Great Dane?). The writing is as random and inconsistent as ever, the characters are still unpleasant and irritating, continue to not act their age, snark at each other, and figure out things either way too easily or not easily enough. They are still so underdeveloped and one-dimensional that I don't know or really care about any of them--some of their full still names haven't even been revealed--and that is a real problem. The writer is trying really hard to raise the stakes, but with the convoluted plot and underwhelming, rushed resolutions to threats, the whole situation just doesn't come across as really that serious.<br /><br />UPDATE 30 May 2012: I can't believe I didn't mention this in my review last year, since it still bugs me to this day. Frollo! Why does he describe Frollo in a way that NO ONE would recognize him?!? It even prompted me to do an illustration of the real Frollo from the film and parks side by side with the character Pearson describes, and they are not at ALL alike. I even sent it to him with a letter describing my disappointment at his disrespect for Disney properties, to which I received a brief and terse reply from his secretary who assured me that he has editors and fact-checkers, which I must most seriously doubt. Now, back to 2011...<br /><br />I'm still having a pretty hard time understanding all the glowing reviews, especially from people who claim to love Disney. True Disney fans should be annoyed and disappointed with these books. I also don't get who this was written for. The author himself said he doesn't consider a specific audience when he writes, but that he focuses on the story. If that's true, I wonder how well his other ventures fare when this focus is required. They were all pretty quick reads, but I spent way too much time going back and trying to figure out when or where something that was later referenced happened, only to find it never did, or it happened differently than described. I'm very sorry if someone put their heart and soul into the work of editing or fact-checking these books, because if they did, it certainly doesn't show. According to Mr. Pearson, this will end up being a seven-book series, but I just can't imagine three more books of this story and these characters. The real reason I secretly hope that these books aren't published is because I'm afraid part of me will feel obligated to read them, since I've come this far. (Hopefully by the time they're released the feeling will have passed.) As for his hoped-for and proposed movie adaptation, I guess I can see a Disney Channel treatment of one or more of them, but they will REALLY need some story and script work before they would work on screen in any capacity. The kids' snarky characters will probably fit in with today's skewed sensibility toward youth media, but that doesn't mean they'll be any good.<br /><br />I think kids and Disney fans deserve a great series with this concept. I also think this is not it. I give this one a generous 2 stars (more like 1 1/2) because I did like seeing more of the characters included, and I still get behind the premise, but the plot is flimsy, the danger is contrived and the resolution is always quick and insultingly simplistic. In the end, these books are glorified fanfiction, riddled with inaccuracies and inconsistency of characters, both new and pre-existing.<br /><br />I think it's time to read some Dickens.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5311082893361010060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText851422192040661283" style="display:none">February 2017 - Well, we finished. He loved it. I sort of hated it. The reader's awful, the plot's full of gaping holes, and the characters are almost offensively stereotypical. The only good part is the setting: Disney!<br /><br />However, my eight year-old son would give it four stars for action, adventure, and Disney. So there you go.<br /><br />November 2016 - Couldn't talk my son into a different audiobook, so I'm listening to this. The first time, five years ago, I didn't finish it. We'll see how it goes this time around. It'll probably take us awhile, since we don't drive together very far during the school year.<br /><br />May 2011 - Doing this on audio.<br /><br />I give up. Good grief, this is awful. Listened to 2 discs and threw in the towel.<br /><br />I LOVE Disney, but I receive more joy from reading the Unofficial Guide to Walt Disney World each year than I do listening to this.<br /><br />Unless you are hardcore Disney, run away from this as fast as you can.</span>

<div id="review_326379703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326379703" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326379703?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326379703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10190460494526832829">Fourth in the Kingdom Keepers children's fantasy series about Disney World and a team of six children who battle the evil Overtakers out to free their evil leaders.<br/><br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>Oops, I think the kids are getting tired of saving Disney World over and over. Certainly they are losing the magic they used to see in it even as many of the Disney characters in the amusement park are pledging their faith in the Kingdom Keepers---and it's about time!<br/><br/>Primarily, this story is about loyalty and honor. Being there</span>
  <span id="freeText10190460494526832829" style="display:none">Fourth in the Kingdom Keepers children's fantasy series about Disney World and a team of six children who battle the evil Overtakers out to free their evil leaders.<br /><br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />Oops, I think the kids are getting tired of saving Disney World over and over. Certainly they are losing the magic they used to see in it even as many of the Disney characters in the amusement park are pledging their faith in the Kingdom Keepers---and it's about time!<br /><br />Primarily, this story is about loyalty and honor. Being there for your friends. It may be scary, but being reliable and responsible take precedence. And slowly, the pool of parents in the know grows.<br /><br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />The adventures had settled down since the kids, the Kingdom Keepers, managed to get Maleficent and Chernabog imprisoned, but now, somehow, something is stealing them one at a time in their sleep. Bringing them over to the Kingdom. And it's not Philby's doing.<br /><br />There has to be some reason the Overtakers are stealing them one by one and it's only together that the Kingdom Keepers will learn the reason and, hopefully, foil their plans. But the Overtakers have thrown in some twists: they're monitoring the kids' computers, recruiting students, and using spells to coerce the Keepers.<br /><br />It's up to the kids. They'll have to explore the park, play the games, deduce the clues, and protect each other. Even as they're chased through the park, crawl through the garbage chutes, steal into the server room, and paddle downriver.<br /><br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Wayne Kresky</strong> is the original Imagineer who came up with the idea of the DHIs and created their ability to come over to the Park in their sleep. <br /><br />The <strong>Kingdom Keepers</strong> are the kids and their DHIs. Disney Host Interactives, a.k.a., Daylight Hologram Imaging. The DHIs are light-generated holograms of the original five kids who act as guides or hosts at Disney World. In return for the use of their images, the kids receive royalties for their college funds and have a perpetual pass to the Parks, HOWEVER, they may only visit at certain times as Disney doesn't want to confuse visitors to the Kingdom with the real kids and their DHIs.<br /><br /><strong>Finn Whitman</strong> has become the Kingdom Keepers' leader while <strong>Charlene Turner</strong> is the "clean cheerleader type' who has finally become comfortable in her role. <strong>Finn's mom </strong>had to be admitted to their secrets and she's been a big help with transportation and eluding Finn's dad. <strong>Isabella "Willa" Angelo</strong> is brilliant with words and has a secret passion for Philby. <strong>Philby</strong> is their computer guru with a backdoor into Disney's data banks who secretly likes Willa. <strong>Terry Maybeck</strong> is the oldest of the group. <strong>Amanda Lockhart</strong> and <strong>Jezebel "Jess"</strong> are Fairlies and still stuck in fostercare with Mrs. Nash. (As fairlies, they had been in a group home where they were constantly tested and probed to explore their powers. Unsurprisingly, they ran away…) Finn and Philby managed to turn them into DHIs so they can utilize their special skills. <strong>Wanda Alcott</strong> is Wayne's daughter and works for Disney. <strong>Aunt Bess "Jelly" Maybeck</strong> is Terry's aunt with whom he lives; she runs a paint-your-own-pottery shop where the kids can meet. <strong>Gladis Philby</strong> is Philby's paranoid mother who has an epiphany. <br /><br /><strong>Greg "Lousy" Luowski</strong>, a fellow student at their school, has a thing for Amanda, but bullies everyone and is perfect as a candidate for a takeover. <strong>Hugo Montcliff </strong>is a friend of Philby's who finds refuge at his home. <strong>Spence Randolph</strong> likes Willa. <strong>Sally Ringwald</strong> is another student at Finn's school. <strong>Dillard Cole</strong> used to be Finn's best friend, before the DHI gig.<br /><br />The <strong>Overtakers</strong> are "a group of fanatical Disney villain characters in the Parks" who are determined to steal the magic and expand their world into the real world. In this installment, the active evil ones are <strong>Snow White's Evil Queen</strong> and <strong>Cruella De Vil</strong>. Suddenly more characters are stepping in, some threatening, some helping. <strong>Judge Claude Frollo</strong> is also on Willa's trail, but she gets help and a lot more from <strong>Ariel</strong>. <strong>Minnie</strong> also helps out, but fears for Mickey. <strong>Jafar</strong> creates a small problem. <strong>Mulan</strong> and <strong>Pluto</strong> are much more helpful.<br /><br /><br /><b>The Cover</b><br />The cover only uses the holographic effect in the title this time. Willa is fleeing the Queen who is preparing to throw a spell at her. The huge sorcerer's hat is in the background with arcs of glittering lights on either side.<br /><br />The title is what it's all about, a <em>Power Play</em> to bring Maleficent and Chernabog back.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10190460494526832829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lauren Asuncion" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34841685-lauren-asuncion"><img alt="Lauren Asuncion" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1191146066?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Asuncion" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Asuncion" href="/user/show/34841685-lauren-asuncion">Lauren Asuncion</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1191146066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5600344898200152927">The story Kingdom Keepers: Power Play is an amazing novel for readers of all ages. This story takes place in Disney World. The main characters are Finn, Willa, Maybeck, Philby, Charlene, Jess, and Amanda. Other characters include Wayne, Wanda, and the overtakers. The characters in this book seem real because along with some of the fantasy problems, they also go through many of the hardships that we go through. We can learn more about characters through their appearance, their speech, and through</span>
  <span id="freeText5600344898200152927" style="display:none">The story Kingdom Keepers: Power Play is an amazing novel for readers of all ages. This story takes place in Disney World. The main characters are Finn, Willa, Maybeck, Philby, Charlene, Jess, and Amanda. Other characters include Wayne, Wanda, and the overtakers. The characters in this book seem real because along with some of the fantasy problems, they also go through many of the hardships that we go through. We can learn more about characters through their appearance, their speech, and through their actions. In my mind, Finn, the main character is an average teenage boy who has blond hair and blue eyes with something about him that makes him seem like the leader of the team. Speech can make a character seem real because it can tell you a lot about their character and personality. An example is when Wayne says, "As you know, these are dangerous times." This shows that Wayne is a man who is cautious and always aware of his surroundings. Another way characters seem real is through their actions. An action that tells us more about Finn is when he steps into a room with two of the most powerful overtakers by himself and ties them up. This tells us that he is brave. I liked this book because I love Disney and because I like books that include fantasy and magic. I highly recommend this book to readers who enjoy books about fantasy, teamwork, action, Disney, and friendship. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5600344898200152927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10245253075561730963" style="display:none"> This book is so much fun. I love how detailed Ridley Pearson described the characters and gave each character time to be recognized. From the beginning to now the characters have grown and you get to know more about them. Though, in this book, the characters' relationships have changed so much and it's so interesting to see the changes in them.<br /> The other thing I love about this book is that the author pulls the Disney characters from your childhood and brings it to life in this book. So many characters, Mickey, Ariel, Judge Frollo, Maleficent, Cruella de Vil, and more! It reminds me of when I was little and makes me want to read the soon-to-come books within the series!<br /> My rating for this book is a 10/10. This book is way better than the other 3 by many reasons. One reason is because of the attachment you have to the characters as they grow and change throughout the book and because of the intense clash of my favorite Disney characters interacting with each other. I would recommend to anyone who loves Disney! :) </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17015783689044815386">I know I have said this before, but if you truely love Disney world, these books are for you.   <span id="freeText17015783689044815386" style="display:none">I know I have said this before, but if you truely love Disney world, these books are for you. I'm not sure I would enjoy them as much if my parents did not take me to Florida enough times that I have each place mapped out and can literally travel with the Keepers through their adventures. <br /><br />Power Play is a bit longer and at times slower than the first three book of the series. However it is the first one where the 'good' characters lend and helping hand. I won't say who the first is, though she is my favorite and can be found in Hollywood Studios, just a hint. More villians turn up, not all jumping on the over taker band wagon. As well as more DHI, not all KK. Pearson is really setting the plot and characters for a BIG battle, bigger than any that have come before or will be seen after.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17015783689044815386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16193271124620891629" style="display:none">That’s right I’m still reading these way past my prime and I’m excited that there’s apparently a new book at the end of this series that I haven’t read yet. My favorite part of these books has to be the text messages, or what the author perceives teenagers to text as (I’m bak instead of I’m back, as though teenagers would honestly cut out one letter) and the illusions to swearing (he said a word Finn would never repeat, etc.) However, since the characters are no longer twelve, these books are getting a little more enjoyable and maybe a tad more relatable (not really but at my age it’s easier to read about 15/16 year olds than 12 year olds) but when I read these the first time when I was the same age as the characters you better believe I thought these books were the best things since sliced bread so i would recommend them for kids that age </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/375209855?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/2810470-christina">Christina</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer375209855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3807226825412511468">I think this book was probably one of the least well written in the series. The kids are now high school age, but the writing still feels low middle school. There needs to be development in writing technique that coincides with the kids growing up...because your audience generally grows too! I can see where there are attempts, but I felt there was much lacking at the end...wasn't satisfied with the climax or character development. They seem unchanging and facing the same problems and reacting th</span>
  <span id="freeText3807226825412511468" style="display:none">I think this book was probably one of the least well written in the series. The kids are now high school age, but the writing still feels low middle school. There needs to be development in writing technique that coincides with the kids growing up...because your audience generally grows too! I can see where there are attempts, but I felt there was much lacking at the end...wasn't satisfied with the climax or character development. They seem unchanging and facing the same problems and reacting the same. Characters should continue to develop - especially when this is a series an not an every book for itself thriller. Still cutesy and fun, I was just hoping for more. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1098531558" />
    <a title="Brian Acevedo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34358318-brian-acevedo"><img alt="Brian Acevedo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431042245p2/34358318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1098531558?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Acevedo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Acevedo" href="/user/show/34358318-brian-acevedo">Brian Acevedo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423153375" href="/book/show/11931954-power-play">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1098531558&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1098531558" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4670871545862682910">Book four in the Kingdom Keepers series was okay. The plot of this book, like books two and three, is strange. It's strange because even after you have finished reading the book, the Keepers are in the same position they were at the end of book three. Understanding of this book definitely requires knowledge of ALL of Walt Disney World. The fact that many people don't possess this knowledge hinders the reading experience. This is one of the books that I actually regret reading. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3249174779" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3249174779" />
    <a title="Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112072399-elena"><img alt="Elena" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3249174779?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena" href="/user/show/112072399-elena">Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3249174779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16689925616377577690">Kingdom Keepers Power Play by Ridley Pearson is an exciting and thrilling novel that has many hidden rassemblements to Disney. The five-kingdom keepers are finally settling down from the wrath of the Overtakers. However, one of the members, Philby, suddenly gets an unexpected FaceTime call while at school. The Kingdom Keepers know now that their lives will no longer be normal. They soon find out that the Overtakers (Disney Villians) are on a mission once again to take over the parks, however thi</span>
  <span id="freeText16689925616377577690" style="display:none">Kingdom Keepers Power Play by Ridley Pearson is an exciting and thrilling novel that has many hidden rassemblements to Disney. The five-kingdom keepers are finally settling down from the wrath of the Overtakers. However, one of the members, Philby, suddenly gets an unexpected FaceTime call while at school. The Kingdom Keepers know now that their lives will no longer be normal. They soon find out that the Overtakers (Disney Villians) are on a mission once again to take over the parks, however this time they first need to set their leaders free. When people around the Keepers start acting strange and changing not only their personality but their eye color, the Keepers realize that things are more complicated than they seem. Now that one of their own might even be in control the Keepers realize that they must be careful with who they trust. There are five Kingdom Keeprtd are Philby, Charlene, Finn, Willa, and Maybeck. Philby is the brains of the groups and can figure out anything that the Overtakers throw at him. Charlene is the athletic one of the group she can always do any aerobics that the team needs. Finn is the leader of the group and is always first to volunteer. Willa is smart, courageous, and kind. Maybeck is strong, tall, and is attractive to all the girls throughout the book. Each of the Keepers has very different personalities providing everyone with someone to connect with.<br />	Throughout the series, I have always felt a connection to Charlene. Similar to Charlene, I am always doing sports or anything to keep myself active. I am also considered the most athletic or my friend group just as Charlene. In this book, people have mistaken Charlene as an Overtaker and her friends won’t tell her everything that they did beforehand. I have felt this way just as Charlene did. One time I can remember that I thought my friends were leaving me out on things and I was upset just as Charlene felt. Having had relatable pieces of my life with herself it has made me better understand the book and helped me put myself in her shoes.<br />	In the Kingdom Keeper series, I have always liked the series. I am a hardcore Disney fan and I love everything Disney but sometimes these books are repetitive. It seems as if the Overtakers are always coming back and the same events are always taking place, making the plot sometimes boring. I feel as though the story is retold with different villains each time. The book is very interesting making you want to keep reading but now as I near the fifth book, I feel as though I keep on reading the same thing. The first two books were incredible and I loved them. However, I don’t feel the draw as much anymore but I still enjoy reading this series.<br />	Though the series has gotten repetitive I still enjoy reading these books for they are easy for me to picture since I have been to Disney many times before. I would recommend this series to people who enjoy anything Disney. This book could be recommended to anyone who has read The Land of Stories. Both of these books contain fictional characters with surrounding villains and characters from famous stories mixed in with present-day people. This book could be read at all ages but because of the length, this book is best fit for kids in late elementary school or middle school. This book is a good read for anyone looking to take their minds to DisneyWorld during their quarantine time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16689925616377577690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pVMegd8Ncqfr7EbqH8frRQfhToe5u/B15lAi1ha3MvY/8CzQ0y29ifHqeA4BJh5Bm5e7qc+mD7JoKLmVYAyipQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('z3Ic8NttSlLSQyKtpaIYa2rdI9SPU0OyN8ix8lzoMhFV0S6h102FfMhFHEm7Q+1v9qvW+vlOvHW5sCqxKlOiQg==')})
  }

Pearson lives with his wife and two daughters, divi</span>
  <span id="freeText1309174929588814441" style="display:none">Ridley Pearson is the author of more than fifty novels, including the <em>New York Times</em> bestseller <em>Killer Weekend</em>; the Lou Boldt crime series; and many books for young readers, including the award-winning children's novels <em>Peter and the Starcatchers</em>, <em>Peter and the Shadow Thieves</em>, and <em>Peter and the Secret of Rundoon</em>, which he cowrote with Dave Barry. Pearson lives with his wife and two daughters, dividing their time between Missouri and Idaho.<br /><br />Also writes Chris Klick mysteries as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/260141.Wendell_McCall" rel="nofollow noopener">Wendell McCall</a>.</span>
